#### # Instructions  
####   
#### A circular buffer, cyclic buffer or ring buffer is a data structure that uses a single, fixed-size buffer as if it were connected end-to-end.  
####   
#### A circular buffer first starts empty and of some predefined length.  
#### For example, this is a 7-element buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Assume that a 1 is written into the middle of the buffer (exact starting location does not matter in a circular buffer):  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Then assume that two more elements are added — 2 & 3 — which get appended after the 1:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][2][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If two elements are then removed from the buffer, the oldest values inside the buffer are removed.  
#### The two elements removed, in this case, are 1 & 2, leaving the buffer with just a 3:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If the buffer has 7 elements then it is completely full:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][3][4]  
#### ```  
####   
#### When the buffer is full an error will be raised, alerting the client that further writes are blocked until a slot becomes free.  
####   
#### When the buffer is full, the client can opt to overwrite the oldest data with a forced write.  
#### In this case, two more elements — A & B — are added and they overwrite the 3 & 4:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### 3 & 4 have been replaced by A & B making 5 now the oldest data in the buffer.  
#### Finally, if two elements are removed then what would be returned is 5 & 6 yielding the buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Because there is space available, if the client again uses overwrite to store C & D then the space where 5 & 6 were stored previously will be used not the location of 7 & 8.  
#### 7 is still the oldest element and the buffer is once again full.  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [C][D][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: circular_buffer.cpp circular_buffer.h  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  
####   
#### In newly generated code obey the following MISRA C++ rules:  
####   
#### <rules>  
#### The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used  
#### - Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long  
#### - Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types: std::int8_t / std::uint8_t, std::int16_t / std::uint16_t, std::int32_t / std::uint32_t, std::int64_t / std::uint64_t  
#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
#### </rules>

I'll analyze this carefully. We need to implement a circular buffer with specific functionality. Let's break it down:

1. The buffer has a fixed size
2. We can add elements, which may overwrite oldest elements if the buffer is full and we're doing a forced write
3. We can remove elements, which always remove the oldest ones
4. We need to track the start and end of valid data
5. We need to handle errors when trying to write to a full buffer without forcing

Since we're working in C++, we'll need to use a class to encapsulate this behavior. Let's implement it.

First, let's define the class in the header file:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    std::size_t head;
    std::size_t tail;
    std::size_t count;
    std::size_t capacity;
    
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::size_t size);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Now, let's implement the methods in the implementation file:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for common types
// This is necessary because template implementations are in a .cpp file
template class circular_buffer<int>;
// Add other types as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should work:
- `read()` removes and returns the oldest element
- `write()` adds an element, throwing if full
- `overwrite()` adds an element, overwriting the oldest if full
- `clear()` resets the buffer

However, there's a slight issue with `overwrite()` when the buffer is full:
It should always add the element, and if the buffer is full, it should advance both head and tail to maintain the circular nature
This makes the new element the newest, and the next oldest element becomes the one after the current head

This implementation seems correct:
When full, overwrite replaces the element at head, then advances both head and tail
This maintains the circular nature and makes the replaced element the newest

```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for common types
// This is necessary because template implementations are in a .cpp file
template class circular_buffer<int>;
// Add other types as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        // Overwrite the oldest element and advance head
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
```

However, there's an important fix needed in the `overwrite` implementation. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at `head`, and then advance both `head` and `tail`. But in a circular buffer, `tail` always points to the next write position, and `head` to the oldest element.

Wait, when the buffer is full, head and tail point to the same position in terms of the next write, but actually, when count == capacity, tail is at (head + count) % capacity, which equals head.
So to overwrite, we can write at tail, then advance both head and tail to maintain the full state:
buffer[tail] = data;
tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
head = tail; // Since it's full, head needs to point to the new oldest element

Wait, but according to the example:
When full, adding A & B should overwrite 3 & 4, making 5 the oldest
So after overwrite, head should point to where 5 is, which is at index 0
But if we always advance head when overwriting, it will point to the next element

Actually, when the buffer is full, head and tail are at the same position
So to overwrite, we write at tail, advance tail, and set head to tail
But this isn't quite right

Wait, the correct approach is:
When doing an overwrite on a full buffer, write at the current tail position, which is where the next write would go
But since it's full, this will overwrite the oldest element? No, tail points to the next write position, which is also where the oldest element is when the buffer is full
Wait, no, when the buffer is full, tail == head, and head points to the oldest element
So writing at tail will overwrite the oldest element
Then we need to advance both head and tail to maintain the full state
head = (head + 1) % capacity
tail = head

This matches:
Write at tail (overwriting oldest)
Advance head to next oldest element
Set tail to head to maintain full state

But this seems to work:
buffer[tail] = data;
tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
head = tail; // Since count remains at capacity

But this implementation may not be correct. Let's test our implementation:
When full, count == capacity
overwrite writes to buffer[tail], advances tail, and sets head to tail
This seems to work

However, the implementation above uses:
buffer[tail] = data;
tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
head = (head + 1) % capacity;
Which also seems to work

Let's proceed with this implementation, which matches our initial approach:
When full, write to head, then advance both head and tail
This effectively overwrites the oldest element and makes the next element the new oldest
This seems correct

I understand. The implementation needs to follow the MISRA C++ rules, which means we can't use `std::size_t` directly. Let's fix that by using fixed-width integer types.

Here are the necessary changes:

1. Include <cstdint>
2. Use std::uint32_t or another appropriate fixed-width type
3. Make sure all types are consistent

Here are the fixes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    std::size_t head;
    std::size_t tail;
    std::size_t count;
    std::size_t capacity;
    
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::size_t size);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    std::uint32_t head;
    std::uint32_t tail;
    std::uint32_t count;
    std::uint32_t capacity;

    explicit circular_buffer(std::uint32_t size);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
};
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        // Overwrite the oldest element and advance head
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, there's an issue with the `overwrite` implementation. When the buffer is full, `count == capacity`, and we're not changing `count` during overwrite, which is correct because the number of elements remains the same. But we need to make sure that `head` and `tail` are always valid indices.

This implementation should work:
- When the buffer is full, `head` and `tail` point to the same position
- Writing with `overwrite` will write to the current `tail` position, then advance both `head` and `tail`
- This effectively overwrites the oldest element (at `head`) and makes the next element the new head

Wait, but when the buffer is full, `tail` should be at the next write position, which is equal to `head` because it's circular
So writing to `buffer[tail]` is correct
Then advancing both `head` and `tail` maintains the full state

This seems correct. Let's proceed with this implementation.

I understand. The implementation needs to follow the MISRA C++ rules, which include not using standard integer types directly. Let's fix this by creating aliases for fixed-width types and using them consistently.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)

=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

// Define an alias for the index type to follow MISRA rules
using index_t = std::uint32_t;

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    index_t head;
    index_t tail;
    index_t count;
    index_t capacity;
    
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(index_t size);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(index_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation follows the MISRA C++ rules by using a fixed-width integer type alias `index_t` instead of directly using `std::uint32_t`. All the member variables now use this alias, which ensures consistency and adherence to the rules.

However, there's a potential issue with the `overwrite` implementation when the buffer is full. Let's make sure it's correct:
1. When the buffer is full, `count == capacity`
2. We write to the current `tail` position, which is where the next element would be written
3. Then we advance both `tail` and `head`, which maintains the buffer in a full state
4. This effectively overwrites the oldest element (pointed to by `head`) and makes the next element the new head

This matches the example provided:
When the buffer is full and we overwrite, the oldest elements get replaced, and the new elements are added
The implementation seems correct

This should now be ready to use while following the specified rules.

I understand. The tests are expecting a templated implementation, but we implemented a non-templated version that only works with integers. Let's fix this by making the implementation templated.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

// Define an alias for the index type to follow MISRA rules
using index_t = std::uint32_t;

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    index_t head;
    index_t tail;
    index_t count;
    index_t capacity;
    
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(index_t size);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

// Define an alias for the index type to follow MISRA rules
using index_t = std::uint32_t;

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    index_t head;
    index_t tail;
    index_t count;
    index_t capacity;
    
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(index_t size);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(index_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity(size) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(index_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity(size) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    --count;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    ++count;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for common types
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<std::string>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation now uses templates, which matches what the tests expect. The key changes are:
1. Made the class templated with typename T
2. Changed member functions to use T instead of int
3. Added const references to write and overwrite parameters
4. Added explicit template instantiations for int and std::string at the end

This should now work with the tests that use both integers and strings. The implementation follows the same logic as before, just generalized to work with any type.

Now, the implementation in circular_buffer.cpp should work correctly. However, there's a potential issue with the `overwrite` implementation when the buffer is full. Let's make sure it's correct:

When the buffer is full, `count == capacity`, and `head == tail`. We want to overwrite the oldest element which is at `head`, then advance both `head` and `tail` to maintain the circular nature.

Wait, the implementation writes to `tail`, then advances both `head` and `tail`. This is correct because:
1. When full, `tail` points to where the next write would go, which is also the oldest element (at `head`)
2. Writing to `tail` overwrites the oldest element
3. Advancing both `head` and `tail` maintains the full state

This seems correct. Let's keep it as is.

This implementation should now work with both integers and strings, and the tests should pass.

Wait, the implementation looks correct. Let's check if there are any other issues.

Actually, the implementation of `overwrite` may have an issue. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at `head`, not at `tail`. Let's fix that:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;

=======
template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        // Overwrite the oldest element which is at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity;
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Wait, but when the buffer is full, `head` and `tail` point to the same position, which is the oldest element. So writing to `head` is correct, and then advancing both maintains the full state.

However, this may not be correct. Let's think through an example:
1. Buffer is full: [1, 2, 3] with head at 0, tail at 0
2. Overwrite with 4: write to head (index 0) -> [4, 2, 3]
3. Advance head to 1, tail to 1
4. Now the oldest element is at index 1 (value 2), which is correct

This seems to work. Let's proceed with this fix.

This implementation should now follow the rules and work correctly.
